Replied To 


for FILE in `influencers.tsv` ; do grep $INFL downloaded_tweets_extend_retweeted_combined.tsv| awk -F "\t" '{print $4}' | tr "," "\n"|sed "s/\"//g" > infl_repliedto/$INFL.hashtags ;done head

for FILE in `ls` ; do for HASHTAG in `cat $FILE`; do count_H_in_C=`grep $HASHTAG $FILE | wc -l` ; count_hashtags_in_C=`cat $FILE | wc -l` ; count_H_entire_dataset=`grep $HASHTAGS ../downloaded_tweets_extend_original_nolf2_repliedto.tsv | wc -l` ; count_hashtags_entire_dataset=7754; frequency_H_in_C=`echo "$count_H_in_C / $count_hashtags_in_C" | bc -l`; frequency_H_overall=`echo "$count_H_entire_dataset / $count_hashtags_entire_dataset" | bc -l` ; relative_frequency_H_C=`echo "$frequency_H_in_C / $frequency_H_overall" | bc -l` ; echo "$HASHTAG $FILE   $relative_frequency_H_C $frequency_H_in_C $frequency_H_overall $count_H_in_C $count_hashtags_in_C $count_H_entire_dataset $count_hashtags_entire_dataset" ; done ; done

for FILE in `ls|grep -v retweets_hashtag_freq.tsv` ; do for HASHTAG in `cat $FILE`; do count_H_in_C=`grep $HASHTAG $FILE | wc -l` ; count_hashtags_in_C=`cat $FILE | wc -l` ; count_H_entire_dataset=`grep $HASHTAG ../downloaded_tweets_extend_retweeted_combined.tsv| wc -l` ; count_hashtags_entire_dataset=148444;  frequency_H_in_C=`echo "$count_H_in_C / $count_hashtags_in_C" | bc -l`; frequency_H_overall=`echo "$count_H_entire_dataset / $count_hashtags_entire_dataset" | bc -l` ; relative_frequency_H_C=`echo "$frequency_H_in_C / $frequency_H_overall" | bc -l` ; echo "$HASHTAG $FILE   $relative_frequency_H_C $frequency_H_in_C $frequency_H_overall $count_H_in_C $count_hashtags_in_C $count_H_entire_dataset $count_hashtags_entire_dataset" ; done ; done > retweets_hashtag_freq.tsv

---------------------------------------------
Solution :

do you see any hashtags that are "special" to some clusters, i.e. that occur often in a particular cluster of tweets, but less often in the tweets overall? Which hashtags and for which clusters (ID'ed by their leaders)? For this purpose, you can sort the rows based on relative_frequency_H_C (higher at top and lower at bottom).

You can learn the topic of a post by looking at the most popular hashtags of a cluster

awk '$8 > 1000 {print $0}' retweets_hashtag_freq_fixed.tsv | sort -n -r -k3 | head -n 10

LA      17379685.hashtags       145.53333333333333343578        1.00000000000000000000  .00687127805771873568   1       1       1020    148444
free    1150476870.hashtags     132.77638640429338108333        1.00000000000000000000  .00753145967502896715   1       1       1118    148444

I applied a filter so that we only looks at hashtags that appeared at least a 1000 times. There were a lot of hashtags that appeared once in their cluster and once in the whole data sets. I wanted to ignore those kinds of hashtags so I put a minimum.  
LA and Free appear pretty frequency in their cluster but in comparison to the whole dataset, is pretty low 

--------------------------------


[bryant@sjsu infl_replies]$ awk '$8 > 50 {print $0}' replies_hashtag_freq.tsv | sort -n -r -k3 | head -n 20
ableg 3008913119.hashtags   117.48484848484848487482 1.00000000000000000000 .00851173587825638380 3 3 66 7754

In the replies dataset, because there were less total hashtags, I didn't expect there to be as much of a bias so I lowered the filter. ableg had one of the higherst relative frequency and a decent number of appearences in the dataset. In this proportion of the data set there are a few hashtags that dominate replies. Hashtags such as Ukraine.
